		<guid isPermaLink="false">https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/blog/?p=52418</guid>

					<description><![CDATA[<p>At Microsoft, building trustworthy AI agents is as critical as building powerful ones. New research from the 2026 Agent Confidence Index shows where teams trust agents today—and why human judgment remains the defining skill in the age of AI.</p>
<p>The post <a href="https://www.microsoft.com/en-us/microsoft-cloud/blog/2026/06/29/the-2026-agent-confidence-index-where-300-builders-see-real-momentum/">The 2026 Agent Confidence Index: Where 300 builders see real momentum</a> appeared first on <a href="https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/blog">Microsoft Azure Blog</a>.</p>
]]></description>
										<content:encoded><![CDATA[
<p class="wp-block-paragraph">A couple of months ago, I sat across from my nine-year-old daughter&#8217;s teachers at a parent-teacher conference. They were kind but concerned. She takes her time on assignments, they said—often deep in thought. How would she do on timed tests next year? I told them I&nbsp;wasn&#8217;t&nbsp;worried. What they described as a problem is, to me, one of the most important things she can learn: the ability to take a hard problem and reason through it from beginning to end. In a world optimized&nbsp;for efficiency, qualities like patience, perseverance, and attention to detail are not deficiencies. They are the foundation of sound judgment, which will&nbsp;become the skills we need most.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">The more time I spend working with AI, the more convinced I become: the question that matters for her future&nbsp;isn&#8217;t&nbsp;how quickly she can answer. It&#8217;s whether she has the judgment to know when an answer can be trusted.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">I’ve&nbsp;spent decades at Microsoft watching this tension play out: first building tools for other developers, then working&nbsp;across AI as models moved from research curiosities to&nbsp;systems&nbsp;deployed&nbsp;at scale. Now we&#8217;re <a href="https://www.linkedin.com/pulse/same-mission-new-chapter-amanda-k-silver-nsgfc/" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">building Microsoft IQ</a>, where we’re&nbsp;exploring&nbsp;how&nbsp;an organization’s collective intelligence can become <a href="https://www.microsoft.com/en-us/ai/microsoft-iq?msockid=06bb933471b660601b26879d700c61c2" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">its greatest advantage</a>. Through every one of those chapters, one thing has remained true: it&#8217;s&nbsp;never enough for a system to be&nbsp;powerful,&nbsp;it&nbsp;must also be trustworthy.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Trust is what turns assistance into delegation.&nbsp;When we can trust an agent to do what we intend, within the limits we set,&nbsp;we can hand off the work we never wanted to spend our lives&nbsp;on: the repetitive tasks that drain attention, the mundane work&nbsp;that fills&nbsp;a day without moving anything meaningful forward, the dangerous work humans should not have to do, the work too vast for any individual or team. Agents should take on that toil, extend our reach, and give us back our time for the work that calls for something only&nbsp;humans&nbsp;bring.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">My daughter&nbsp;doesn&#8217;t&nbsp;know any of this yet. But by the time she&#8217;s grown, most&nbsp;of the work that rewards speed and repetition will be work we delegate.&nbsp;What will matter&nbsp;then is exactly what gave her teachers pause: the&nbsp;patience&nbsp;to stay with a hard problem, reason through it, and decide&nbsp;when&nbsp;she’s&nbsp;reached&nbsp;a conclusion she can trust. The very thing&nbsp;they&nbsp;feared&nbsp;might&nbsp;hold her back&nbsp;could be&nbsp;exactly what the next era prizes most.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">So no,&nbsp;I&#8217;m&nbsp;not worried about the timed test. I&nbsp;hope&nbsp;she grows up in a world where software carries the&nbsp;toil&nbsp;and people are freed&nbsp;for&nbsp;the work that is unmistakably ours—to think, to&nbsp;judge,&nbsp;to&nbsp;create,&nbsp;to&nbsp;care for one another. That is the future I want agents to make&nbsp;real.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">But&nbsp;my&nbsp;hope is not&nbsp;evidence&nbsp;it will happen. The future I just described turns&nbsp;on&nbsp;a single question: can we trust agents to do the work? Trust is earned one task at a time. So, I went looking for&nbsp;evidence&nbsp;of where it&#8217;s been earned, and where it hasn&#8217;t.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">For the past year, the conversation around AI agents has circled the same promise:&nbsp;eliminate&nbsp;toil so people can focus on what matters. But I&nbsp;keep coming back to sharper questions.&nbsp;What,&nbsp;exactly,&nbsp;is toilsome? Where does&nbsp;toil&nbsp;actually live in people’s work? What are the technical leaders closest to this shift willing to hand&nbsp;off—and what gives them the confidence to do it? To find out, we <a href="https://www.technologyreview.com/2026/06/29/1139635/agent-confidence-on-the-technical-frontier/" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">partnered with MIT Technology Review Insights</a>&nbsp;on new research that draws directly from the people building this frontier. Not the people talking about it,&nbsp;the people doing it. We surveyed 300 technical experts across AI, data, and cloud domains, spanning 12 industries and 4 regions of the world, asking them to rank their confidence across 101 of the top tasks. What we got back is&nbsp;the <a href="https://aka.ms/MITinsightreport" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">2026 Agent Confidence Index</a>,&nbsp;an honest map of where agents are delivering real value, so our community can see&nbsp;what’s&nbsp;working and move forward together with conviction.</p>



<div class="wp-block-buttons is-content-justification-center is-layout-flex wp-container-core-buttons-is-layout-a89b3969 wp-block-buttons-is-layout-flex">
<div class="wp-block-button"><a class="wp-block-button__link wp-element-button" href="https://aka.ms/agentconfidenceindex" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer noreferrer noopener">Explore the 2026 Agent Confidence Index report</a></div>
</div>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="learn-from-where-confidence-is-highest"><strong>Learn from where confidence is highest</strong></h2>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Across the 101 tasks measured, average confidence already lands at&nbsp;<strong>64 out of 100</strong>, and thirty tasks clear 70. The highest scores cluster on work that is both predictable and draining: the late nights, the interruptions, the low-value repetition. Automated report generation leads at 83.5. Boilerplate code generation for new features sits at 82.5, the hours a developer no longer spends rewriting the same patterns, freed for the work that challenges them. Certificate expiration monitoring and renewal, at 81.5, ends the scramble that pulls engineers off high-stakes problems for something entirely routine. Real-time data stream monitoring follows at 80.5, and release note generation from commit history at 79.5, the manual end-of-sprint commit review, gone. This is where frontier teams are already delegating to agents, regularly.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">The pattern holds across every discipline. In developer and AI workflows it extends to API client maintenance and code identification; in cloud operations, to ticket routing and cost optimization; in data, to anomaly detection. Wherever it sits in the stack, this is work technical teams now trust agents to own.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">What matters most here isn&#8217;t what the data says about the tasks, it&#8217;s what it says about the people delegating them. When technical experts believe in something deeply enough to hand it real work, that belief ripples outward. It becomes the recommendation they make to their leadership, the solution they build for their customers, and the culture they create for their teams.</p>



<figure data-wp-context="{&quot;imageId&quot;:&quot;6a4370d566bd8&quot;}" data-wp-interactive="core/image" data-wp-key="6a4370d566bd8" class="wp-block-image aligncenter wp-lightbox-container"><img decoding="async" data-wp-class--hide="state.isContentHidden" data-wp-class--show="state.isContentVisible" data-wp-init="callbacks.setButtonStyles" data-wp-on--click="actions.showLightbox" data-wp-on--load="callbacks.setButtonStyles" data-wp-on-window--resize="callbacks.setButtonStyles" src="https://www.microsoft.com/en-us/microsoft-cloud/blog/wp-content/uploads/2026/06/word-image-15364-2-2.png" alt="Chart showing trending AI agent tasks across AI, data, and cloud workflows. Scores indicate strong confidence in automation for reporting, monitoring, code generation, and cloud operations tasks." class="wp-image-15378" /><button

		</button></figure>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="even-the-toughest-agent-tasks-are-gaining-traction"><strong>Even the toughest agent tasks are gaining traction</strong></h2>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Here&#8217;s what strikes me most: the tasks ranked lower on <a href="https://aka.ms/agentconfidenceindex">the index</a> are still high in absolute terms. Service mesh configuration and troubleshooting sits at 37.5, database schema migration scripting at 46.5, memory leak detection at 48.5. These sit at the very frontier, the interconnected, high-stakes work where investment and innovation are concentrated right now.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Consider what they demand. Service mesh configuration touches many systems at once. Database migration carries real stakes, requiring precision across data, application, and infrastructure layers at the same time. Memory leak detection means diving deep into a system&#8217;s behavior under load, accounting for conditions that shift from one deployment to the next. These are the challenges that have separated great engineers from exceptional ones—and even here, experts see agents helping. Not carrying the work alone, but contributing where it used to be unthinkable. That confidence is still climbing, and that&#8217;s telling.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">We&#8217;re shipping new capabilities constantly to support this momentum. Database migration tooling in <a href="https://github.com/features/ai/github-app">GitHub Copilot</a> now covers not just scripts but the full application and infrastructure migration story. The <a href="https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/products/sre-agent">Azure Site Reliability Engineering (SRE) Agent</a> brings decades of experience operating Azure at scale and deep profiling capabilities directly into memory analysis and performance diagnosis.</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="why-human-judgment-remains-paramount"><strong>Why human judgment remains paramount</strong></h2>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">When we asked technical experts how they&#8217;re navigating agent adoption, <strong>59% named &#8220;keeping humans in the loop&#8221; as their top priority</strong>—ahead of better observability, ahead of governance documentation, and ahead of everything else. That&#8217;s a mark of maturity. Teams moving forward with clarity treat agent oversight as non-negotiable, regardless of how capabilities evolve.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">The boundary itself is straightforward. Agents excel at well-specified, high-volume, reversible work: they synthesize data, automate known workflows, and surface anomalies at a speed and scale no human team could match. The moment a decision becomes high-stakes, context-dependent, or hard to undo, a human signs off. That isn&#8217;t a limitation of the technology, it&#8217;s the architecture of a trustworthy system.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">What&#8217;s changing, and what remains underappreciated, is the skill it takes to draw that boundary well: the discipline of <a href="https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/foundry/how-to/evaluate-generative-ai-app">full-lifecycle evaluations</a> and <a href="https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/foundry/guardrails/guardrails-overview">guardrails</a>. Success means measuring agent output against intent and keeping behavior inside your business strategy. It&#8217;s new territory for most engineering teams, and it&#8217;s becoming table stakes for modern software faster than most organizations realize. The good news: the same tools generating the work can help you build the harness. <a href="https://docs.github.com/en/copilot/concepts/agents/github-copilot-app">Ask GitHub Copilot</a> to write the evals and it will. Frontier teams are already doing this, and it&#8217;s why they&#8217;re pulling ahead.</p>


<figure data-wp-context="{&quot;imageId&quot;:&quot;6a4370d567ed4&quot;}" data-wp-interactive="core/image" data-wp-key="6a4370d567ed4" class="wp-block-image aligncenter wp-lightbox-container"><img decoding="async" data-wp-class--hide="state.isContentHidden" data-wp-class--show="state.isContentVisible" data-wp-init="callbacks.setButtonStyles" data-wp-on--click="actions.showLightbox" data-wp-on--load="callbacks.setButtonStyles" data-wp-on-window--resize="callbacks.setButtonStyles" src="https://www.microsoft.com/en-us/microsoft-cloud/blog/wp-content/uploads/2026/06/word-image-15364-3-2.webp" alt="MIT Technology Review Insights survey chart titled &ldquo;Concerns are addressed by keeping humans in the loop and increasing observability.&rdquo; Respondents most frequently identified keeping humans in the loop (59%) and increasing observability/monitoring and tracing (53%) as key ways to address concerns around AI agents. Other approaches include creating privacy-governed documentation (42%), upskilling within one&rsquo;s craft (36%), addressing security and access control (33%), API and framework standardization (25%), identifying and communicating ROI (25%), scaling personal potential (16%), and accessing ecosystem support (11%)" class="wp-image-15379 webp-format" srcset="" data-orig-src="https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/blog/wp-content/uploads/2019/02/1bbe5959-0e2e-4309-8079-3a71ce986e5e.webp"><button

			</svg>
		</button></figure>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="agents-are-opening-career-doors-for-engineering">Agents are opening career doors for engineering</h2>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Across system reliability and site operations, evaluations and quality assurance, and data pipeline management, <strong>80% or more of respondents see meaningful career opportunity ahead</strong>. We believe this is one of the most significant moments in the history of building software, not because agents replace what technical people do, but because what&#8217;s left when they take on the toil is the work that defines a career: the judgment calls, the architectural vision, the reasoning to navigate complexity under pressure. That fluency will define the next generation of technical leadership.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">We&#8217;re living this shift at Microsoft, right alongside our customers. Junior developers are using agents to explore codebases on their own and arriving at mentoring conversations with sharper, more sophisticated questions. Senior engineers are covering more ground because the repetitive work that used to fill their days is now delegated, and the work that&#8217;s left is harder, more interesting, and more consequential. Both are growing into more capable versions of themselves. For me, that&#8217;s the outcome I&#8217;ve always believed technology could deliver.</p>



<figure data-wp-context="{&quot;imageId&quot;:&quot;6a4370d56f352&quot;}" data-wp-interactive="core/image" data-wp-key="6a4370d56f352" class="wp-block-image aligncenter wp-lightbox-container"><img decoding="async" data-wp-class--hide="state.isContentHidden" data-wp-class--show="state.isContentVisible" data-wp-init="callbacks.setButtonStyles" data-wp-on--click="actions.showLightbox" data-wp-on--load="callbacks.setButtonStyles" data-wp-on-window--resize="callbacks.setButtonStyles" src="https://www.microsoft.com/en-us/microsoft-cloud/blog/wp-content/uploads/2026/06/word-image-15364-4-2.png" alt="MIT Technology Review Insights survey chart showing confidence that AI agents will enhance careers across technology disciplines. <h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="an-integrated-approach-to-intelligence-and-trust"><strong>An integrated approach to intelligence and trust</strong></h2>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Designing more sophisticated agent systems has made one thing clear: agents thrive in well-integrated environments, working best when your whole stack draws on a single source of truth. The high-confidence tasks are the ones we&#8217;ve already figured out; the meaningful frontier is the harder, interconnected work,  and that&#8217;s exactly where observability, governance, security, and unified intelligence have to operate as one.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph"><a href="https://www.microsoft.com/en-us/ai/microsoft-iq" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Microsoft IQ</a> brings your <strong>enterprise context into a</strong> <strong>single, continuous intelligence layer</strong>. Within it, <a href="https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/microsoft-365/copilot/extensibility/work-iq/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Work IQ</a> builds semantic understanding of how your business operates across email, calendar, meetings, chats, files, people, and collaboration patterns. Such depth of knowledge is the reason technical teams choose us and it’s what drives my focus and passion in learning how people actually work so their agents get them. My colleague Kim Manis, CVP of Product for Microsoft Fabric, has <a href="https://aka.ms/Confidence-Index-Data-Blog" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">written specifically about what this means for data professionals</a>, and the integral role of <a href="https://www.microsoft.com/en-us/microsoft-fabric/features/iq" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Fabric IQ</a>.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">It’s all part of the <a href="https://blogs.microsoft.com/blog/2026/06/02/ai-alone-wont-change-your-business-the-system-running-it-will/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Microsoft Agent Platform</a>, which is becoming <strong>the operating system for enterprise AI at scale</strong>. From building in <a href="https://github.com/features/copilot" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">GitHub</a> and contextualizing with <a href="https://www.microsoft.com/en-us/ai/microsoft-iq?msockid=06bb933471b660601b26879d700c61c2" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Microsoft IQ</a>, to running in <a href="https://devblogs.microsoft.com/foundry/agent-service-build2026/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Microsoft Foundry</a> and governing in <a href="https://aka.ms/BUILD_SecurityBlog" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Microsoft Agent 365</a>, Microsoft is uniquely positioned to help customers bring together data, models, agents, and human judgment into a continuously improving and secure system.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Frontier transformation is being led by builders like you.</p>



<h3 class="wp-block-heading" id="next-steps"><strong>Next steps:</strong></h3>



<ul class="wp-block-list">
<li class="wp-block-list-item">Download <a href="https://aka.ms/MITinsightreport" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">The 2026 Agent Confidence Index</a> from our partners at MIT Technology Review Insights.It is a free, ungated deep dive into all 101 tasks, broken out by role and workflow, with the patterns and reasoning behind where confidence is strongest and the frontier is expanding.</li>



<li class="wp-block-list-item">Join us at the <a href="https://www.ai.engineer/worldsfair/2026" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">AI Engineering World’s Fair</a> (June 29-July 2) where our very own <a href="https://www.linkedin.com/in/pabloc/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Pablo Castro</a> will keynote, and our teams will offer <a href="https://www.ai.engineer/worldsfair/schedule?q=Microsoft&amp;view=list" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">16 breakout sessions and 4 labs</a>. Swing by the Microsoft booth as well to explore an interactive 3D visualization of the Index data. We want to hear what’s working for you right now.</li>



<li class="wp-block-list-item">Learn more about <a href="https://www.microsoft.com/en-us/ai/microsoft-iq" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Microsoft IQ</a> and how it connects across <a href="https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/microsoft-365/copilot/extensibility/work-iq/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Work IQ</a>, <a href="https://www.microsoft.com/en-us/microsoft-fabric/features/IQ" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Fabirc IQ</a>, <a href="https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/foundry/agents/concepts/what-is-foundry-iq?tabs=portal" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Foundry IQ</a>, and the newly announced <a href="https://www.microsoft.com/en-us/webiq?msockid=06bb933471b660601b26879d700c61c2" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Web IQ</a>. You can catch up on all the developer innovation from Microsoft Build through <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=FFMm454fxNA" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Satya Nadella’s keynote</a>, <a href="https://blogs.microsoft.com/blog/2026/06/02/microsoft-build-2026-be-yourself-at-work/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Kyle Daigle’s blog post</a>, and the <a href="https://github.com/microsoft/Build-CLI" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Microsoft Build CLI</a>.</li>

										<content:encoded><![CDATA[
<aside class="table-of-contents-block accordion wp-block-bloginabox-theme-table-of-contents" id="accordion-4d5d3d08-b5a7-4dd6-b747-00ddee77346d" data-bi-aN="table-of-contents">

		</svg>
	</button>
	<div id="accordion-collapse-4d5d3d08-b5a7-4dd6-b747-00ddee77346d" class="table-of-contents-block__collapse-wrapper collapse show" data-parent="#accordion-4d5d3d08-b5a7-4dd6-b747-00ddee77346d">
		<div class="table-of-contents-block__content">
			<ol class="table-of-contents-block__list"><li class="table-of-contents-block__list-item"><a class="table-of-contents-block__list-item-link" href="#speed-up-ai-and-data-intensive-workloads">Speed up AI and data-intensive workloads</a></li><li class="table-of-contents-block__list-item"><a class="table-of-contents-block__list-item-link" href="#scale-cloud-native-applications-with-shared-storage">Scale cloud-native applications with shared storage</a></li><li class="table-of-contents-block__list-item"><a class="table-of-contents-block__list-item-link" href="#modernize-enterprise-applications-with-less-disruption">Modernize enterprise applications with less disruption</a></li><li class="table-of-contents-block__list-item"><a class="table-of-contents-block__list-item-link" href="#build-more-with-partners-and-isvs">Build more with partners and ISVs</a></li><li class="table-of-contents-block__list-item"><a class="table-of-contents-block__list-item-link" href="#azure-files">Azure Files</a></li></ol>		</div>
	</div>
	<span class="table-of-contents-block__progress-bar"></span>
</aside>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Linux workloads are evolving quickly as organizations modernize on-premises Linux applications, adopt cloud-native architectures, and build new AI and data-intensive pipelines in the cloud. As this shift accelerates, teams need a managed file platform that delivers the performance, resilience, security, and flexibility required to support these workloads in Azure.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph"><a href="https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/products/storage/files" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Azure Files</a> helps teams make that transition with fully managed file storage for Linux workloads. It combines familiar file access with built-in performance, data protection, security, and Azure service integration, making it easier to run shared file storage in the cloud without managing file infrastructure directly.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">In this blog, we explore how <a href="https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/storage/files/files-nfs-protocol">Azure Files NFS</a> supports modern Linux workloads across AI, cloud-native, enterprise modernization, and partner or ISV scenarios.</p>



<div class="wp-block-buttons is-content-justification-center is-layout-flex wp-container-core-buttons-is-layout-a89b3969 wp-block-buttons-is-layout-flex">
<div class="wp-block-button"><a class="wp-block-button__link wp-element-button" href="https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/storage/files/files-whats-new" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">What&#8217;s new with Azure Files</a></div>
</div>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="speed-up-ai-and-data-intensive-workloads">Speed up AI and data-intensive workloads</h2>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">AI inferencing is where a trained model is loaded and serves predictions. Before any request is answered, the model&#8217;s weights, which capture what the model learned during training, must be read from storage into the serving instance. As models have grown to tens or hundreds of gigabytes, that loading step heavily influences how quickly an endpoint starts and scales. It happens every time a replica spins up, and because GPUs are among the most expensive resources in the stack, every minute they sit idle waiting on weights is money wasted.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Traditionally, teams embed model weights directly in the container image or have each replica download its own copy—producing bloated images, duplicated data, and cold starts that stretch to minutes just when an inference fleet needs to scale fast. With Azure Files, the weights live once on a file share that every replica mounts and reads simultaneously: images stay lean, there&#8217;s a single copy to manage, and new replicas come online in seconds for small and mid-sized models. Support for the Linux NFS <a href="https://learn.microsoft.com/azure/storage/files/nfs-performance#nfs-nconnect"><em>nconnect</em> mount option</a> allows a client to establish multiple parallel TCP connections to the same file share, which can improve throughput at scale. </p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">The <strong>new</strong> <a href="https://learn.microsoft.com/azure/storage/files/zonal-placement?tabs=azure-portal">Zonal placement</a> lets you co-locate file shares in the same availability zone as your GPU virtual machines, reducing round-trip latency for the data-intensive reads these workloads depend on. The <a href="https://learn.microsoft.com/azure/storage/files/understanding-billing#provisioned-v2-model">provisioned v2 billing model</a> lets you size IOPS and throughput independently to keep GPUs fed. The result is faster scaling, higher GPU utilization, lower cost per inference, and a more responsive experience for your customers.</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="scale-cloud-native-applications-with-shared-storage">Scale cloud-native applications with shared storage</h2>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Cloud-native applications often need shared storage that works directly with Kubernetes-based deployment models. This is especially important for workloads that need ReadWriteMany (RWX) access, persistent shared state, or storage that evolves with the application.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Azure Files integrates with Azure Kubernetes Service through the <a href="https://learn.microsoft.com/azure/aks/create-volume-azure-files">Azure Files CSI driver</a>, enabling Kubernetes-native workflows such as dynamic provisioning through StorageClasses, expandable persistent volumes, and shared storage across multiple pods with ReadWriteMany access.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">The cloud-native story is also about scale and speed. The <a href="https://learn.microsoft.com/azure/storage/files/storage-files-planning#management-concepts"><strong>new</strong> file share experience</a> supports up to 10,000 file shares per subscription per region, helping teams support large multi-tenant or high-density environments. It also provisions about 2.5 times faster, with even greater gains in batch deployments, making it easier to scale shared storage quickly as application demand grows. The provisioned v2 model also helps teams manage total cost of ownership as they scale: you can start with smaller shares, grow capacity incrementally as demand rises, and use percentage-based metrics to monitor utilization and right-size shares over time.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Together, these capabilities make Azure Files well suited for cloud-native scenarios such as shared content repositories, configuration and artifact stores, CI/CD workflows, and containerized services that need persistent file storage across replicas or nodes.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph"><a href="https://www.microsoft.com/en/customers/story/1376275735613758956-zooniverse-azure-non-profit">Zooniverse</a>, the world’s largest platform for people-powered research, puts this into practice. After migrating from AWS to a fully managed Azure Kubernetes Service environment, the team runs self-hosted Redis instances backed by Azure Files to provide caching and persisted data storage. The platform supports roughly 100 active projects and 10,000 to 15,000 daily users, with traffic that can spike to tens of thousands of API calls per minute. Deployments that once took an hour now run in three to 10 minutes, and the move to managed services on Azure reduced the team’s operational workload by about one full-time engineer.</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="modernize-enterprise-applications-with-less-disruption">Modernize enterprise applications with less disruption</h2>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Many enterprise applications built on NFS still depend on familiar Linux and POSIX-style behaviors, stable file semantics, and operational continuity. That makes wholesale refactoring expensive and risky.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Azure Files helps organizations modernize these applications by providing managed NFS file shares for Linux workloads while preserving familiar access patterns. That makes it easier to move existing Linux line-of-business applications like SAP and other workloads that depend on POSIX-compliant file shares, case sensitivity, or Unix-style permissions without forcing teams to refactor them first.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Organizations can use the <strong>new </strong><a href="https://learn.microsoft.com/azure/storage/files/migrate-files-storage-mover">Azure Storage Mover</a> and <a href="https://learn.microsoft.com/azure/storage/files/storage-files-migration-nfs?tabs=ubuntu">Azure Migrate support for NFS</a> to assess, plan, and move Linux-based file workloads into Azure with less disruption to existing operations. Teams that prefer their existing tooling can also run third-party migrations from on-premises NAS using partners such as Komprise, giving Linux file estates more than one path into Azure. The result is a practical, end-to-end path for bringing existing Linux and NFS environments into Azure, where assessment, migration, and modernization happen as one motion rather than a series of disconnected steps.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Once applications are running in Azure, organizations can also strengthen business continuity and security. Features such as <a href="https://learn.microsoft.com/azure/storage/files/storage-snapshots-files?tabs=portal#nfs-file-share-snapshots">snapshots</a> and <a href="https://learn.microsoft.com/azure/storage/files/storage-files-prevent-file-share-deletion?tabs=azure-portal">soft delete</a> help improve recovery options and protect business-critical data, while <a href="https://learn.microsoft.com/azure/storage/files/encryption-in-transit-for-nfs-shares?tabs=azure-portal%2CUbuntu">encryption in transit for NFS</a> helps secure data moving between clients and shares. Combined with Azure networking options such as <a href="https://learn.microsoft.com/azure/storage/files/storage-files-configure-s2s-vpn?tabs=azure-portal">VPN and ExpressRoute</a>, Azure Files provides resilience, and operational foundation enterprises expect for long-running Linux applications.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">The <a href="https://learn.microsoft.com/azure/storage/files/create-file-share?tabs=azure-portal"><strong>new</strong> file share experience</a> also simplifies governance, improves cost tracking at the share level, and enables more granular network configuration and role-based access control for different teams and applications.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph"><a href="https://www.microsoft.com/en/customers/story/25243-medline-azure" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Medline</a>, an over $25 billion leader in medical-surgical supply manufacturing and distribution, shows this modernization path in action. As part of its migration from an on-premises SAP ECC on HANA environment to Azure, Medline built a cloud-native SAP solution leveraging fully managed Azure Files shares to provide zonally resilient shared storage. The re-architecture improved transaction times for key SAP workloads by more than 80 percent, cut response times for the most essential transactions by nearly 60 percent, and accelerated IDoc processing by more than 50 percent.</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="build-more-with-partners-and-isvs">Build more with partners and ISVs</h2>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">A key reason Azure Files fits partner ecosystems is that it speaks standard protocols rather than a proprietary interface. By exposing industry-standard SMB 3.x and NFS 4.1 endpoints, Azure Files works with existing applications, tools, and frameworks without code changes.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Azure Files NFS also expands what partners, ISVs, and platform teams can build on top of the service. Capabilities such as the NFS Snapshot, Soft Delete, and <a href="https://learn.microsoft.com/rest/api/storageservices/file-service-rest-api">REST API</a> for NFS shares help ecosystem partners integrate Azure Files into broader solutions for BCDR, data movement, management, and application enablement.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">In the SaaS and ISV space, Azure Files can also serve as shared storage behind partner applications that need familiar POSIX-style access patterns without forcing customers to manage file infrastructure themselves. These same protocol and data-protection primitives also make Azure Files a target for database backup workloads—including SAP and Oracle backups—that partners and ISVs increasingly run against NFS or REST endpoints.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Azure Files also fits into adjacent developer and platform scenarios. For example, <strong>new </strong><a href="https://learn.microsoft.com/azure/aks/github-actions-azure-files-overview">GitHub-based workflows on Azure Kubernetes Service</a> may use shared storage for runners, caching, artifacts, or job state. These scenarios show how Azure Files can bring together application platforms, developer tooling, and shared file storage.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Across AI, cloud-native, enterprise, and ecosystem scenarios, Azure Files NFS gives organizations a single managed file platform for modern Linux workloads. It helps teams support shared storage needs in Azure without stitching together separate solutions for each use case. To get started, explore <a href="https://learn.microsoft.com/azure/storage/files/">Azure Files documentation</a>. If you would like to learn more or discuss your scenario, contact us at <a href="mailto:azurefiles@microsoft.com">azurefiles@microsoft.com</a>.</p>

<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Run shared file storage in the cloud without managing file infrastructure directly.</p>

		<title>The performance dividend: Optimizing PostgreSQL on Azure directly in Visual Studio Code</title>
		<link>https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/blog/the-performance-dividend-optimizing-postgresql-on-azure-directly-in-visual-studio-code/</link>
					<comments>https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/blog/the-performance-dividend-optimizing-postgresql-on-azure-directly-in-visual-studio-code/#respond</comments>
		
		<dc:creator><![CDATA[Jesse Sullivan]]></dc:creator>
		<pubDate>Fri, 26 Jun 2026 17:00:00 +0000</pubDate>
				<category><![CDATA[Databases]]></category>
		<category><![CDATA[Hybrid + multicloud]]></category>
		<category><![CDATA[PostgreSQL]]></category>
		<category><![CDATA[Visual Studio]]></category>
		<guid isPermaLink="false">https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/blog/?p=52298</guid>

					<description><![CDATA[<p>Poor database performance is never just a database problem. In enterprise teams, it shows up as missed SLAs, delayed releases, frustrated development teams, and rising operational risk. The performance problem compounds further in business impact, often resulting in frustrated customers, retention and conversion risk, and lost revenue.</p>
<p>The post <a href="https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/blog/the-performance-dividend-optimizing-postgresql-on-azure-directly-in-visual-studio-code/">The performance dividend: Optimizing PostgreSQL on Azure directly in Visual Studio Code</a> appeared first on <a href="https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/blog">Microsoft Azure Blog</a>.</p>
]]></description>
										<content:encoded><![CDATA[
<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Poor database performance is never just a database problem. In enterprise teams, it shows up as missed service-level agreements (SLAs), delayed releases, frustrated development teams, and rising operational risk. The performance problem compounds further in business impact, often resulting in frustrated customers, retention and conversion risk, and lost revenue.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">I have seen this repeatedly while working with enterprises building and running large‑scale data platforms, both as a customer and partner, and now with Microsoft. When teams are forced to jump between SQL editors, monitoring dashboards, cloud portals, and documentation just to diagnose a slow query, the real cost is not just technical. It&#8217;s also time, trust, and momentum lost across the business.</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="a-more-integrated-way-to-run-postgresql-on-azure">A more integrated way to run PostgreSQL on Azure</h2>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">This is why I am optimistic about where PostgreSQL on Azure stands today. Microsoft’s investment in open source and PostgreSQL has matured significantly over the last several years. <a href="https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/products/postgresql" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Azure Database for PostgreSQL</a> has evolved into a fully managed, fully open-source enterprise-ready platform, <a href="https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/products/horizondb" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Azure HorizonDB</a> has entered the conversation as the next-gen Postgres on Azure delivering 3x faster performance than self-managed Postgres, and Microsoft is extending that value directly into the tools developers and database administrators (DBAs) already use. The PostgreSQL extension for Visual Studio Code is a clear example of that progress, especially with its new performance‑enhancing capabilities.</p>



<div class="wp-block-buttons is-style-medium is-content-justification-center is-layout-flex wp-container-core-buttons-is-layout-a89b3969 wp-block-buttons-is-layout-flex">
<div class="wp-block-button is-style-default"><a class="wp-block-button__link wp-element-button" href="https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/products/postgresql" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Try PostgreSQL on Azure</a></div>
</div>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Most enterprise teams do not lack tooling. They lack integration. Performance work often breaks down because insights live in one place, actions live in another, and context is lost in between. Microsoft’s direction with the PostgreSQL extension for VS Code focuses on closing those gaps by bringing development, diagnostics, and tuning into a single workflow.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">The extension is designed to help teams manage PostgreSQL across the full lifecycle, from authoring queries and exploring schemas to monitoring server health and optimizing performance. For organizations standardizing PostgreSQL on Azure, this creates a more coherent operating model that reduces friction between developers, DBAs, and platform teams.</p>



<div class="wp-block-buttons is-content-justification-center is-layout-flex wp-container-core-buttons-is-layout-a89b3969 wp-block-buttons-is-layout-flex">
<div class="wp-block-button"><a class="wp-block-button__link wp-element-button" href="https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/postgresql/development/vs-code-extension/postgresql-extension-overview" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer noreferrer noopener">Learn more about the PostgreSQL extension for VS Code</a></div>
</div>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="seeing-performance-clearly-with-the-server-metrics-dashboard">Seeing performance clearly with the Server Metrics Dashboard</h2>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">One of the most impactful additions is the <a href="https://github.com/microsoft/vscode-pgsql/discussions/157">server metrics dashboard</a>. For DBAs and platform engineers, this dashboard brings key performance signals such as CPU, memory, storage, and connections directly into VS Code. Instead of switching contexts to investigate an issue, teams can view metrics where they already work.</p>



<figure data-wp-context="{&quot;imageId&quot;:&quot;6a4370d57d70b&quot;}" data-wp-interactive="core/image" data-wp-key="6a4370d57d70b" class="wp-block-image size-full wp-lightbox-container"><img fetchpriority="high" decoding="async" width="1280" height="720" data-wp-class--hide="state.isContentHidden" data-wp-class--show="state.isContentVisible" data-wp-init="callbacks.setButtonStyles" data-wp-on--click="actions.showLightbox" data-wp-on--load="callbacks.setButtonStyles" data-wp-on-window--resize="callbacks.setButtonStyles" src="https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/blog/wp-content/uploads/2026/06/metrics-dashboard-1.gif" alt="Scrolling through high C P U no index dashboard." class="wp-image-52357" /><button
			class="lightbox-trigger"
			type="button"
			aria-haspopup="dialog"
			aria-label="Enlarge"
			data-wp-init="callbacks.initTriggerButton"
			data-wp-on--click="actions.showLightbox"
			data-wp-style--right="state.imageButtonRight"

			</svg>
		</button></figure>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Because the dashboard is integrated with Azure, it provides Azure‑specific telemetry and historical insights that help teams understand trends, not just snapshots. When performance issues arise, the time from detection to investigation is significantly reduced.</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="from-insight-to-action-with-azure-advisor-in-vs-code">From insight to action with Azure Advisor in VS Code</h2>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Observability only matters if it leads to action. The PostgreSQL extension surfaces <a href="https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/postgresql/configure-maintain/concepts-azure-advisor-recommendations" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Azure Advisor</a> recommendations directly in the editor, connecting performance insights with concrete guidance. These recommendations can include suggestions around configuration, indexing, and resource optimization based on Azure telemetry.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">For enterprise teams, this shortens the feedback loop. Instead of manually correlating metrics with best practices, teams receive contextual recommendations aligned to their actual workloads. This improves operational confidence and helps standardize tuning practices across environments.</p>



<div class="wp-block-buttons is-content-justification-center is-layout-flex wp-container-core-buttons-is-layout-a89b3969 wp-block-buttons-is-layout-flex">
<div class="wp-block-button"><a class="wp-block-button__link wp-element-button" href="https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/postgresql/configure-maintain/concepts-azure-advisor-recommendations" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer noreferrer noopener">Optimize your resources with Azure Advisor</a></div>
</div>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="faster-diagnosis-with-query-plan-visualization-and-ai-assistance">Faster diagnosis with Query Plan visualization and AI assistance</h2>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Performance tuning often comes down to understanding query behavior. Recent improvements to the extension enhance query plan visualization, making execution plans easier to interpret during troubleshooting and optimization.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Beyond visualization, Microsoft is embedding AI‑assisted query analysis and optimization directly into the workflow. Developers and DBAs can analyze query plans, understand potential bottlenecks, and explore optimization options without leaving VS Code. This does not replace deep PostgreSQL expertise, but it helps teams move faster and make better decisions earlier in the development cycle.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">These capabilities are especially valuable for enterprise environments where not every developer is a PostgreSQL specialist, yet performance expectations remain high.</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="better-authoring-experiences-reduce-performance-issues-upstream">Better authoring experiences reduce performance issues upstream</h2>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Performance work does not start in production. It starts when schemas are designed and queries are written. The PostgreSQL extension improves this experience with schema‑aware IntelliSense, search_path‑aware query authoring, and reliable object explorer behavior for large and complex databases.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Developers can write, run, and refine SQL with better context, while DBAs benefit from more consistent and predictable interactions with large schema estates. Improvements to object explorer reliability also matter at enterprise scale, where long‑running sessions and frequent refreshes are common.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">
  Combined with <a href="https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/postgresql/security/security-entra-configure">Microsoft Entra ID</a> authentication and integrated Azure resource discovery, the extension provides a secure and governed way to work with PostgreSQL across development and production environments.
</p>



<div class="wp-block-buttons is-content-justification-center is-layout-flex wp-container-core-buttons-is-layout-a89b3969 wp-block-buttons-is-layout-flex">
<div class="wp-block-button"><a class="wp-block-button__link wp-element-button" href="https://learn.microsoft.com/en-us/azure/postgresql/development/vs-code-extension/quickstart-connect-query?tabs=vscode" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer noreferrer noopener">Try PostgreSQL extension for VS Code</a></div>
</div>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="from-tuning-to-performance-payout">From tuning to performance payout</h2>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Taken together, these capabilities change the day‑to‑day experience of <a href="https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/products/postgresql" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">running PostgreSQL on Azure</a>. Azure Database for PostgreSQL already delivers the managed fundamentals enterprises expect, including high availability, security, and best‑practice guidance. The PostgreSQL extension for VS Code extends that value into execution by making performance management part of the same workflow as development.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">This integration is a practical differentiator. It reflects an understanding of how enterprise teams actually work and where time is lost today. Instead of adding more tools, Azure is tightening the loop between insight and action.</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="a-look-ahead-ai-native-postgresql-with-azure-horizondb">A look ahead: AI‑native PostgreSQL with Azure HorizonDB</h2>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">As enterprises look toward AI‑native architectures, Microsoft is also introducing <a href="https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/products/horizondb" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Azure HorizonDB in public preview</a>. Azure HorizonDB is designed for cloud‑native, AI‑ready PostgreSQL‑compatible workloads that require advanced scalability and integrated AI capabilities.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">For most production workloads today, <a href="https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/products/postgresql" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Azure Database for PostgreSQL</a> remains the recommended choice. <a href="https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/products/horizondb" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Azure HorizonDB</a> represents an adjacent, forward‑looking option for teams exploring what comes next for their AI‑powered applications.</p>



<div class="wp-block-buttons is-content-justification-center is-layout-flex wp-container-core-buttons-is-layout-a89b3969 wp-block-buttons-is-layout-flex">
<div class="wp-block-button"><a class="wp-block-button__link wp-element-button" href="https://youtu.be/dl98C_Pgne8?si=AkCFSut74YwdDWVh" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Watch video: Azure HorizonDB + VS Code: Your AI App Development Workspace</a></div>
</div>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="turning-performance-into-a-competitive-advantage">Turning performance into a competitive advantage</h2>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">The real advantage of these new capabilities is the way they come together to reduce friction, improve clarity, and help teams act faster. For enterprises managing PostgreSQL at scale, that translates directly into better reliability, faster delivery, and lower operational risk.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">If you are running PostgreSQL on Azure today, now is a good time to see what this looks like in practice. Try the PostgreSQL extension for VS Code and connect it to your Postgres databases on Azure to diagnose issues faster, optimize performance with greater confidence, and keep critical workloads running the way your business and your customers expect.</p>

<p class="wp-block-paragraph">What if your cloud environment could help you move from insight to action in real time, with systems already working through the next set of decisions?</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">As applications scale across hybrid infrastructure, microservices, and AI workloads, leading organizations are moving toward operating models where insight flows directly into action as part of an ongoing, system-driven loop.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">This is where agentic cloud operations comes in. Agentic cloud operations is an approach in which AI-powered agents—guided by user intent—continuously observe, reason, and assist with actions across the cloud lifecycle. Signals are not treated as isolated events. They are input into coordinated workflows that evolve over time, helping improve performance, cost, and reliability as systems run.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">According to <a href="https://aka.ms/AgenticOps-MaterialWhitepaper" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">recent research conducted with Material</a>, 79% of organizations are already deploying agentic AI in production, reflecting how quickly this model is becoming part of how cloud environments are operated.</p>



<div class="wp-block-buttons is-content-justification-center is-layout-flex wp-container-core-buttons-is-layout-a89b3969 wp-block-buttons-is-layout-flex">
<div class="wp-block-button"><a class="wp-block-button__link wp-element-button" href="https://aka.ms/AgenticOps-MaterialWhitepaper" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Explore the research findings</a></div>
</div>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="governance-connects-insight-to-action">Governance connects insight to action</h2>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">To operate this model, governance needs to be built directly into how cloud operations run. Observability provides a continuous stream of signals and context, but those signals only become useful when they can drive action in a controlled and consistent way. As agents begin to take on more responsibility across detection, investigation, and remediation, every action should be designed to follow human-defined policies, respect access controls, and remain aligned with organizational intent.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">At Microsoft Build, this emerged as a key requirement. Developers and IT need governance embedded within the same workflows that connect observability to optimization. As insights trigger actions, those actions remain constrained, auditable, and repeatable across environments.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Our vision for agentic operations includes a shared operating model that brings observability and optimization together, where insights lead directly to action and every action is governed by built‑in policy and control, with humans always in the loop. In Azure, we’re building a system in which observability, governance, and optimization work together. Signals are continuously interpreted, actions are applied within policy boundaries, and outcomes feed back into the system to guide the next decision.</p>



<figure data-wp-context="{&quot;imageId&quot;:&quot;6a4370d58288b&quot;}" data-wp-interactive="core/image" data-wp-key="6a4370d58288b" class="wp-block-image aligncenter size-large wp-lightbox-container"><img decoding="async" width="1280" height="720" data-wp-class--hide="state.isContentHidden" data-wp-class--show="state.isContentVisible" data-wp-init="callbacks.setButtonStyles" data-wp-on--click="actions.showLightbox" data-wp-on--load="callbacks.setButtonStyles" data-wp-on-window--resize="callbacks.setButtonStyles" src="https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/blog/wp-content/uploads/2026/06/PetalGraphicSVG.svg" alt="Diagram showing a human-in-the-loop governance model for agentic cloud operations, with Create, Deploy, Govern, Secure, and Operate connected in a continuous cycle around a central review and approval process." class="wp-image-52286" /><button
			class="lightbox-trigger"
			type="button"

				<path fill="#fff" d="M2 0a2 2 0 0 0-2 2v2h1.5V2a.5.5 0 0 1 .5-.5h2V0H2Zm2 10.5H2a.5.5 0 0 1-.5-.5V8H0v2a2 2 0 0 0 2 2h2v-1.5ZM8 12v-1.5h2a.5.5 0 0 0 .5-.5V8H12v2a2 2 0 0 1-2 2H8Zm2-12a2 2 0 0 1 2 2v2h-1.5V2a.5.5 0 0 0-.5-.5H8V0h2Z" />
			</svg>
		</button></figure>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="observability-is-the-intelligence-layer">Observability is the intelligence layer</h2>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">As cloud environments expand, telemetry and alerts have outpaced what teams can manage through manual processes alone. Engineers often spend significant time correlating signals, validating issues, and understanding what changed.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">In an agentic model, observability aims to provide continuous intelligence. It gives AI agents the context they need to identify meaningful signals, understand dependencies across the environment, and surface relevant insights early. Observability helps answer what is happening and why, with greater clarity and timeliness.</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="from-signals-to-resolution">From signals to resolution</h2>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Building on this foundation, the <a href="http://aka.ms/ObservabilityAgentGA" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Azure Copilot observability agent</a>, now generally available, brings this intelligence into day-to-day operations. The observability agent can continuously analyze telemetry across your environment, including application topology, dependencies, and baseline behavior. When an issue begins to emerge, it can identify patterns, begin investigation, and provide context before teams start their analysis.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Agentic observability changes how incidents are handled in practice. Issues can be surfaced earlier, with related signals already grouped to reduce noise. Investigations can begin automatically, tracing dependencies across services to help identify likely root causes. Teams are provided with clear, contextual recommendations that support faster decision-making. </p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Observability also extends to AI workloads, so agents, services, and infrastructure can be viewed together. The result helps enable more consistent flow from detection to understanding to action, with less manual effort required along the way.</p>



<blockquote class="wp-block-quote has-quote-default-font-size is-layout-flow wp-block-quote-is-layout-flow">
<p class="wp-block-paragraph">The biggest value is speed&#8230; The observability agent helps us resolve incidents faster and reduce operational overhead&#8230; we’ve reclaimed an estimated 250 engineering hours monthly.</p>
<cite>—Narmada Krishnaswamy, Head of KPMG Audit Application Support and Operations</cite></blockquote>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Observability provides a clearer view of what is happening. It also creates the foundation for the next step. Observability answers the most urgent question in cloud operations: what&#8217;s happening, and why? But for organizations operating at scale, that’s only the beginning.</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="optimization-becomes-continuous">Optimization becomes continuous </h2>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">When observability provides consistent, real-time context, it can be used to guide ongoing improvement.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Microsoft defines optimization as the continuous practice of improving cloud workloads across cost, performance, resilience, and sustainability. In an agentic model, optimization becomes part of everyday workflows rather than a separate, periodic activity.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">At FinOps X 2026, many organizations shared that AI is introducing new cost dynamics. Usage patterns are more variable, less predictable, and often tied to rapid changes in workloads. This makes it harder to rely on periodic reviews and traditional cost management approaches. Optimization must happen closer to where decisions are made.</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="from-dashboards-to-connected-workflows">From dashboards to connected workflows</h2>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">As optimization becomes more integrated, the way work gets done also evolves. Instead of switching between tools and dashboards, teams can interact with systems through guided workflows. Agents help estimate costs before resources are created, apply governance guardrails automatically, monitor usage patterns, and surface potential issues earlier.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">For example, during development, cost implications can be surfaced before deployment, along with relevant policy guidance. As systems run, patterns in usage can be monitored and changes can be investigated with supporting context. When opportunities for improvement are identified, agents can help prioritize and guide next steps. This approach helps bring cost, performance, and efficiency considerations into the flow of work in a more consistent way.</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="optimization-intelligence-across-tools-and-environments">Optimization intelligence across tools and environments</h2>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">To support this model, Microsoft is extending cost and usage intelligence beyond the Azure portal into the tools teams already use.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">The Azure Resource Manager MCP Server, now in public preview, enables AI agents to access cost and usage data through a standardized interface. This allows cost insights to appear within developer environments, copilots, and custom workflows without requiring custom integrations. </p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">As a result, developers can build with greater awareness of cost implications, and operations teams can investigate and optimize using natural language interactions. Workflows can be applied more consistently across teams and environments.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Multi-step processes such as estimation, investigation, and optimization can also be organized into reusable workflows, helping teams scale these practices.</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="bringing-it-all-together-in-a-closed-loop-system">Bringing it all together in a closed loop system </h2>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">Observability and optimization are increasingly connected. Observability provides continuous context. Agentic AI helps interpret signals and support actions. Optimization reflects the outcomes of those actions over time, guided by governance and policy. This creates a system where insights can more directly inform the next step, and where each action contributes to ongoing improvement. Over time, this supports more consistent operations across environments and teams.</p>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph">In this model, progress comes from acting with better context and greater consistency. Microsoft is helping organizations adopt this approach by connecting people, data, and tools through <a href="https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/products/copilot" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Azure Copilot</a> and related capabilities. Teams gain the ability to resolve issues more efficiently, apply optimization continuously, and operate with governance built in.</p>



<h2 class="wp-block-heading" id="get-startedtosee-how-these-capabilities-come-together-in-practice-you-can-explore-and-try-them-across-your-environment">Get started with Azure</h2>



<p class="wp-block-paragraph" id="get-startedtosee-how-these-capabilities-come-together-in-practice-you-can-explore-and-try-them-across-your-environment">To see how these capabilities come together in practice, you can explore and try them across your environment:</p>



<ul class="wp-block-list">
<li class="wp-block-list-item"><a href="https://azure.microsoft.com/en-us/products/copilot">Azure Copilot</a>
<ul class="wp-block-list">
<li class="wp-block-list-item">An AI-powered assistant that helps translate operational signals into guided actions across your cloud environment.</li>
</ul>
</li>



<li class="wp-block-list-item"><a href="http://aka.ms/ObservabilityAgentGA" target="_blank" rel="noreferrer noopener">Azure Copilot observability agent (generally available)</a>
<ul class="wp-block-list">
<li class="wp-block-list-item">Identify root causes and accelerate resolution through continuous analysis and assisted investigation.</li>
</ul>
</li>



<li class="wp-block-list-item"><a href="https://github.com/Azure/Azure-Resource-Manager-MCP/blob/main/docs/CostManagementAndPricingTools.md">Azure FinOps MCP Server (public preview)</a>
<ul class="wp-block-list">
<li class="wp-block-list-item">Connect cost and usage intelligence into agent workflows, developer tools, and custom environments through an open interface.</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
